  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_910fb5b7-59f0-48f4-8c07-988293a06d2b'
      });

But the dark shadows that have preyed on the Clan for many moons still lurk just beyond the forest. Soon a mysterious visitor will walk in one cat's dreams, whispering promises of greatness, with results that will change the future of ThunderClan in ways that no cat could have foreseen.</span>

If all the books were free, then the authors wouldn't have an<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You can't read the books on Goodreads - you have to buy them, or find them in a library. If all the books were free, then the authors wouldn't have any money to write more :(<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113573637?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/4062909-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer113573637&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113573637" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4842496762362180936">This was a very good book! I was always at the edge of my seat! I was dissapointed that Tigerstar is training Ivypaw. I had a feeling something like that would happen! I am glad he isn't training Dovepaw. Jayfeather is doubting his ability as a medicine cat I think. Leafpool was a great medicine cat and I don't think she is doing a very good job at being a warrior. Or at least I think she is definitely better at being a medicine cat. Is it just me, or do other people wish that LionBlaze and Jayf</span>
  <span id="freeText4842496762362180936" style="display:none">This was a very good book! I was always at the edge of my seat! I was dissapointed that Tigerstar is training Ivypaw. I had a feeling something like that would happen! I am glad he isn't training Dovepaw. Jayfeather is doubting his ability as a medicine cat I think. Leafpool was a great medicine cat and I don't think she is doing a very good job at being a warrior. Or at least I think she is definitely better at being a medicine cat. Is it just me, or do other people wish that LionBlaze and Jayfeather should forgive Leafpool and Squirrelflight? Or at least talk to them? I also think that Squirrelflight and Brambleclaw should get back together. They were an awesome couple! I sorta wished that more things would of happened in between the big things that happened. Sometimes I just wanted to skip ahead to get to a more exciting part. But, all in all, it was a very good book and I think the next one will be too! Erin Hunter is very good at description and she paints an amazing picture! So I was very satisfied with this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4842496762362180936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_97026619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97026619" />
    <a title="Sarah705" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3107503-sarah705"><img alt="Sarah705" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97026619?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah705" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah705" href="/user/show/3107503-sarah705">Sarah705</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97026619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17157886823747651564">Wow, that was really exciting. There was so much doubt and so many secrets, and I really think that that had to do with the author's message. Dovepaw and Ivypaw, who used to tell each other everything, have lost so much trust! They each have an important secret to keep, and their secrets are really tearing them apart from each other.<br/><br/>I love my sister, and it's hard for me to keep even a small secret from her. I can't imagine what it would be like to have to hide everything from her. When it comes</span>
  <span id="freeText17157886823747651564" style="display:none">Wow, that was really exciting. There was so much doubt and so many secrets, and I really think that that had to do with the author's message. Dovepaw and Ivypaw, who used to tell each other everything, have lost so much trust! They each have an important secret to keep, and their secrets are really tearing them apart from each other.<br /><br />I love my sister, and it's hard for me to keep even a small secret from her. I can't imagine what it would be like to have to hide everything from her. When it comes down to it, I really think I'd rather tell her everything. Having a close sibling is like having a best friend. They're always there for fun and support. But best friends also fight. Siblings can't always get along, and they don't.<br /><br />Family is complicated, and Dovepaw and Ivypaw aren't the only example of that in this book. Jayfeather and Lionblaze feel so much hatred towards Leafpool and Squirrelflight, their mother and aunt. Jayfeather is disgusted with the idea of a medicine cat going against the rules and having babies. because of that he hates his mother, and tries to avoid her as much as possible. But in the time that he does spend with her, I can tell that not only does she love and miss him, but he loves her to.<br /><br />Sometimes loving someone makes them easier to hate. I'm sure that I'm not the first one to realize that, but it's absolutely true. When you really have strong feelings for someone, it's easier for those feelings to turn negative than to just disappear.<br /><br />Jayfeather also finds out that Yellowfang had a son who she killed. Killing your own child seems crazy and inexcusable, but I can kind of understand it. Being Brokenstar's mother, Yellowfang obviously cared for him. Even though she loved him at first, he was a mistake. She wasn't supposed to have children. So when he turned evil, it was easy for her to misinterpret that love as hate. It was easier to kill him than to live with him, so that's what she did.<br /><br />Although it worked out for Yellowfang, I'm not saying that you should kill your family members, even if they do bug you. What I'm really trying to say, and what I think the author was trying to say, is that family may be complicated, but hurting eachother doesn't help anything. The more you push your family away, the harder it will be to deal with them. There are no rules when it comes to love, but it's even harder when it's with your family. There's no escape, so you ultimately just have to learn to deal with them.<br /><br />Even when your family feels impossible, the best way to deal with them is just to express what you're feeling. As shown by Dovepaw and Ivypaw, even when you feel really far from them, they'll always be there for you when you need them. Secrets don't help anything, and they really only make family more complicated. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17157886823747651564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7328058859403328164">I used to feel that each book in the Warriors series had one main part per book, as in one major thing happened and that was it. In Omen of the Stars, though, there is action throughout-- this makes them better than each of the previous series' books, in my opinion.<br/><br/>Fading Echoes has excitement throughout all of its 300 plus pages.   <span id="freeText7328058859403328164" style="display:none">I used to feel that each book in the Warriors series had one main part per book, as in one major thing happened and that was it. In Omen of the Stars, though, there is action throughout-- this makes them better than each of the previous series' books, in my opinion.<br /><br />Fading Echoes has excitement throughout all of its 300 plus pages. I loved this book because there wasn't just one major event, like there is in Power of Three and The New Prophecy. Fading Echoes is unique because it has so much character development with a majority of its large cast. The revelation about Ivypaw was my favorite part of this book, along with the climax at the end. <br /><br />Warriors has a great writing style, and there is a good balance between the cats of ThunderClan and their stories compared to the rest of the cast. I loved Fading Echoes and I can't wait to read Night Whispers and the rest of this series.</span>

                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9292490581153493690">Premise: "After the sharp-eyed Jay and the roaring Lion, peace will come on Dove's gentle wing…" These words given by StarClan to ThunderClan apprentice Dovepaw now make sense to her. She is one of the three cats mentioned in the great prophecy, along with the warrior Lionblaze and the medicine cat Jayfeather. They vow to use their gifts to protect all the Clans from a coming darkness. But that same darkness that haunts one apprentice seduces another, and not even the Three realize how a spark o</span>
  <span id="freeText9292490581153493690" style="display:none">Premise: "After the sharp-eyed Jay and the roaring Lion, peace will come on Dove's gentle wing…" These words given by StarClan to ThunderClan apprentice Dovepaw now make sense to her. She is one of the three cats mentioned in the great prophecy, along with the warrior Lionblaze and the medicine cat Jayfeather. They vow to use their gifts to protect all the Clans from a coming darkness. But that same darkness that haunts one apprentice seduces another, and not even the Three realize how a spark of envy can be fanned into a flame of destruction.<br /><br />Story/Writing: Geez! These books can get intense but that was one of the most intense books I've read in a long time! As always, the Erin Hunter team does a phenomenal job building up things that initially don't seem to matter much but end up proving extremely important later on in the story. For example, in the prologue, we see Tigerstar and his cohorts taking advantage of Breezepelt's grudge against his half-siblings. That was expected. But I didn't think he could instigate such a devastating battle by persuading just two apprentices to do his dirty work! In another example, early on we see ThunderClan warriors and apprentices training in the trees, and they use that tactic in the climactic battle in the end! I'm so excited about how mind-blowingly well this is written and built up that I can barely put it in words! But I'll try anyway! In all seriousness, when I looked back at how everything builds up to the climax at the end of this book, my jaw hit the floor! This book alone is a testament to how much time and care and especially planning the authors can put into their stories. Everything leads so organically and naturally into another thing that I seriously didn't see it coming. By the end of it all, I was just in a state of shock, the same way I suppose Lionblaze was. Just completely and utterly dumbfounded! But of course, even great ideas have to be written well in order to be executed well. And the tone is just perfect. It feels dramatic without being ridiculously sentimental. It feels intense without the feeling that it's all being done for shock value. It keeps you guessing, but not too much. And it ends on a cliffhanger without making it feel tacked on! I seriously want to know how the main players (at least) manage to make sense of all this, if they do at all! Peace has always been a fragile thing between the Clans, but now it feels like it's been broken forever. This vicious, no-holds-barred fight between ThunderClan and ShadowClan didn't feel like a simple battle between Clans (though no battle is simple); this was something else. These two Clans are not going to be able to mend relations between them for a long, long time… And I LOVE it! I wanna read more but at the same time I don't 'cause I don't know how things can get any worse than they are now.<br /><br />Characters: Man, what a great cast of characters – good, bad, and somewhere in between, as well as old and new! These well-written characters seriously do pull most of this story's weight and play a huge part in making it work so well. They are cats, but they and especially their interactions with each other feel so real and relatable! The way they talk and deal with certain things feels very human and like something you would read in any other book (the good ones, anyway) with human characters. They have all sorts of struggles, regrets, and strong emotions but at the same time, they would not fit in a soap-opera – these are hardcore feral warriors and they prove that in this book time and time again!<br /><br />Dovepaw – While a lot of the doubts I may have had about Dovepaw not being a Mary Sue were swept away with the river in "The Fourth Apprentice," here, any remaining ones were smashed to smithereens. To Ivypaw, the grass may look greener on Dovepaw's side, but Ivypaw doesn't know about the hard work her sister puts in to keep her own grass green. In other words, Dovepaw may be special, but she is not without struggles. And I mean real struggles! Not to mention they fit her age. She makes an embarrassing screw-up by visiting WindClan, even though she had good intentions; she and Tigerheart are starting to like each other, but he refuses to confide in her; she wants to use her power but at the same time she doesn't – in that she wants to use it to help people but she doesn't want to spy on anyone; and worst of all, she's forced to be distant from the cat she's always been closest to – her sister – so now their relationship is suffering as well. Even if she hasn't gone through as much as some other characters (at least, not yet) these are still some pretty heavy issues for her. But it's the way she deals with them, while also considering her age, that makes her a great character. Same with her power. It's how she uses it (and doesn't use it) that truly matters. She's not even a warrior yet and already she has to take on a ton of responsibility. And honestly, she handles it better than I think most adult warriors would. She'll always come to her Clan's rescue but she's not an indiscriminate killer. She's kind but will also make her opinion known if need be, whatever everyone else thinks. And her power proves it can be a weakness as well as a strength. I really felt for her when she got such sensory overload in the final fight that she can barely fight at all. And you can feel her innocence ebbing away as she's forced to witness how truly violent a battle can be, especially when she's supposed to fight cats she knows and likes. That said, she's come this far without getting broken, and I look forward to seeing her not just survive but thrive!<br /><br />Ivypaw – Since she and her sister have roughly the same amount of time narrating the story through their respective points of view, and since she's on the cover, and since she didn't feature all that much in "The Fourth Apprentice," I think it's only fair that I give as much attention to her as Dovepaw. And I suspect that would be how she'd like it! In this book, Ivypaw goes through a character arc pretty similar to Lionblaze's. That said, it does make sense and it does feel like her own story. You can tell throughout the book that she loves her sister very much. But unfortunately, it often proves to be the case that the more we love someone the more that person can hurt us. While she was wrong for being envious of Dovepaw, I did feel some sympathy towards her. She doesn't get to see Dovepaw that much anymore; Dovepaw is often away with her mentor or even Firestar; Dovepaw is quite a bit more favored and more skilled than her; and Dovepaw is keeping secrets from her. I was nibbling my nails when I read about her first encounter with Hawkfrost. But by the time Tigerstar persuaded her to lie to Firestar, and persuaded her so easily, I was freaking out. After she did lie to Firestar, when I had to read a bit more about Briarlight, I was thinking, "Ugh! I don't care about Briarlight! …Well, yes I do. But this is way more important!" But now the battle has been fought, that prey has been killed and eaten. It was awful to read, and I seriously hope she eventually sees the error of her ways and realizes how phenomenally she screwed up! And even if that is the case, I know how unlikely it is that Dovepaw will take it all lightly. That all said, I still like Ivypaw too much to lose her to the Dark Forest. She really does have the potential to be a great warrior and I would hate for it to be wasted!<br /><br />Lionblaze – Once again, Lionblaze feels like he's really matured and grown since the previous title featuring him. Dovepaw obviously couldn't have a better mentor than Lionblaze, given that they're two of the Three. And he's as committed as ever to his Clan, though that might prove to be his downfall as well. After all, he did kill Russetfur at the end (Or did he?), and allowed his usual hunger to fight on behalf of his Clan to get the better of him. That said, I was rooting for him nonstop when he led alongside Firestar the operation to retrieve Longtail's body and rescue Briarlight from the wreckage of the tree when it fell into the hollow. I also can tell that he and Cinderheart might soon be a thing! Speaking of which, if anyone can help Ivypaw escape Tigerstar's influence, it's him, given he had an almost identical experience.<br /><br />Jayfeather – One of my favorite medicine cats in this series is just as cool and interesting as ever! He's now come to respect Mothwing, despite her lack of belief in StarClan. I felt for him when he mourned the loss of his ancient stick. The scene where he and Squirrelflight have a heavy discussion on the way to ShadowClan felt needed and touching. And I rooted for Jayfeather just as much as Lionblaze when the former committed himself to helping Briarlight adjust to her new and sadly permanent dilemma. While not the most affectionate cat, he's always been a medicine cat. And just like it is for doctors in real life, he hates giving his patients bad news about their condition. I was also oddly rooting for him when he had the nerve to go willingly into the Dark Forest on purpose, even if he did have two (and then one) StarClan warriors with him. Not to mention he manages to stand up to Tigerstar while keeping himself on his paws!<br /><br />Various Other Characters – Oh, Tigerstar…you savage, monstrous, crow-food eating beast of a cat! When I realized at the end of this book how he pretty much instigated the climactic battle between ThunderClan and ShadowClan, thereby ruining any chances of good relations between the two Clans (at least in the near future), I was forced to admit that Tigerstar is not just physically intimidating but a strategic, calculating master of manipulation. From the beginning, we're shown how he seems to always know just the right buttons to push in order to turn potentially any cat to his side. He wields such massive influence over Ivypaw and Tigerheart, and with such ease, it's unbelievable. Not to mention it really made me nervous. Considering how terrible the climactic battle in this book was, and that this book was only the second one in this arc, I'm left to wonder how much more havoc he can wreak before he makes his final move. Speaking of which, just as I like Ivypaw too much to see her turn evil, I feel that way just as much toward Tigerheart! He's so likable and he and Dovepaw are so cute together (different Clans aside), even if he doesn't tell her why he's leaving ShadowClan scent on the ThunderClan border. I daresay he has the potential to surpass his grandfather as an example for all future ShadowClan cats to look up to. And speaking of ShadowClan, I haven't felt this bad for them since "Yellowfang's Secret." This battle couldn't have happened at a worse time, nor could the outcome have been any worse, especially for them. Their deputy is dead and they've lost important territory (important to them, anyway). I seriously hope Littlecloud doesn't hold too much of a grudge toward Jayfeather over this, given how much of a help the former was to the latter regarding Briarlight. Speaking of whom, wow does she prove to be a champ! And so soon! I admire the authors for having the gall to give this character, especially one who's a cat, an injury as bad as this. She'll never be a warrior, she'll never hunt and fight, nor will she ever have kits. But she's really shown herself to be strong and determined, dedicated to Jayfeather's treatments for her and always at least trying to look on the bright side (hence her name). Even if she ultimately failed to save Longtail's life, I hope her injury reminds her Clan of the selflessness behind her attempt. It was awesome to really see Yellowfang and Spottedleaf again, and not just in cameos. They're in on the action, brief though it was. And I honestly wasn't surprised that it was Yellowfang who made the decision to go into the Dark Forest in the first place, given how bold and daring she was in life. Not to mention her brief showdown with Brokenstar was so tension-filled, given that this tyrannical cat was her son. As for Firestar, he will always be one of my favorite characters in this series, but he can sometimes be just as flawed as some others. Even so, I like that. It makes him feel more believable as a character. He says he doesn't make important decisions without reason, but he bets this battle with ShadowClan on an apprentice's dream and didn't consult his medicine cat about it. I only hope he's learned from this, just as I hope he recovers in the shortest amount of time possible from losing yet another life. That said, he FINALLY knows that Lionblaze, Jayfeather, and Dovepaw are the cats in the prophecy! I knew he'd find out sooner or later, but still…! If anything, it's kinda impressive the secret managed to be kept hidden for this long.<br /><br />Overall: This book was a fantastic second volume in the "Omen of the Stars" arc, especially in how it sets up the villain and how much of a threat he truly is on his own. I was so invested in the characters and their struggles and dilemmas and the climactic battle was an absolute thrill ride! I know this is gonna have a huge ripple effect on the rest of the books in this arc, and I can't wait to read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9292490581153493690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6795550728630405824" style="display:none">This book was pure awesomeness, just like I expected!!! Jayfeather, Lionblaze, and Dovepaw try to figure out the impending prophecy more. and a lot of things happen to the Clans - like a fallen tree that kills Longtail and makes Briarlight unable to feel her hind paws anymore. <div id="review_159060609" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159060609" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4460586-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159060609?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/4460586-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer159060609&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159060609" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2854597235031890341">CATS!!!!!!! Haha, yes cats, warrior cats no less!!!!!!! I love this series only problem its quite hard to write a review since the series is so long, there are so many characters, and the only way you really understand the books is if you read all the books in the correct order! But to make it short and sweet so you don't have to read all the books I will describe the basic issue of this book. Dovepaw, Lionblaze, and Jayfeather have discovered that there is trouble coming. Trouble not even Starc</span>
  <span id="freeText2854597235031890341" style="display:none">CATS!!!!!!! Haha, yes cats, warrior cats no less!!!!!!! I love this series only problem its quite hard to write a review since the series is so long, there are so many characters, and the only way you really understand the books is if you read all the books in the correct order! But to make it short and sweet so you don't have to read all the books I will describe the basic issue of this book. Dovepaw, Lionblaze, and Jayfeather have discovered that there is trouble coming. Trouble not even Starclan can keep at bay. And even with the power of the stars in their paws they could still be doomed! What is the threat?? Well the Dark Forest (the place bad cats go when they die, the opposite of Starclan) is rising to power, and are doing the unthinkable! Training cats from clans to fight for them. No clan is safe from the Dark Forest cats. They proved to have power over the clans when the book ended with Shadowclan and Thunderclan having a battle over a boundary dispute. The Dark Forest's most feared cat, Tigerstar convinced an apprentice, Ivypaw (Dovepaw's sister) to lie to her clan leader Firestar. Lying about having a dream regarding land that Thunderclan had given to Shadowclan as a gift. But with this fake dream proposed by an apprentice sent by the Dark Forest comes nothing but pain and loss. Almost every cat is injured and two cats die. Firestar loses a life. And the Shadowclan deputy died. After this terrible battle with lost lives over a crappy piece of, Jayfeather senses more trouble. And he is right things will only get worse...Clans will be divided, Starclan will be divided, and the cats of the Dark Forest will try to rise to power!!!!!!!!<br /><br />This was an amazing book, and I already started the next one! If you LOVE animals, and esp. cats! You will love these books! Erin Hunter is an awewsome author! :) Can't wait to finish her next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2854597235031890341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_139933532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139933532" />

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139933532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4995198993302727033">In Fading Echoes, Dovepaw and Ivypaw; the main cats in the 4th series, learn more of the ways of the wild, and Dovepaw discovers her power to hear anything. At the same time, Shadowclan is plotting against Thunderclan to steal their territory, and the book ends with the clans battling each other in a great battle. Afterward, the cats learn The Dark Forest is trying to break the clans up, and the book ends there. Its a great book and a great series, an I recommend it to everyone.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S+Cem8w93z1AlnbnzdmUw0Ze2X32Nyq8uB3BXfyPPIifrfyxH31jpnj2Ms7ri7SG5AqhCTpBxLvTgkRYw5E9sw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  <span id="freeText2131257327769866398" style="display:none">Erin Hunter is the pseudonym of five people: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/132369.Kate_Cary" title="Kate Cary" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Cary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220345.Cherith_Baldry" title="Cherith Baldry" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherith Baldry</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/374504.Tui_T__Sutherland" title="Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Tui T. Sutherland</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2742182.Gillian_Philip" title="Gillian Philip" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Philip</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/769868.Inbali_Iserles" title="Inbali Iserles" rel="nofollow noopener">Inbali Iserles</a>, as well as editor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/645010.Victoria_Holmes" title="Victoria Holmes" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Holmes</a>. Together, they write the Warriors series as well as the Seekers and Survivors series. Erin Hunter is working on a new series now called Bravelands. <br /><br />Erin Hunter is inspired by a love of cats and a fascination with the ferocity of the natural world. As well as having a great respect for nature in all its forms, Erin enjoys creating rich mythical explanations for animal behavior, shaped by her interest in astronomy and standing stones.</span>
